data-uotrack=\"InlineShareCommentsBtn\"><span class=\"inline-share-count inline-share-count-comments\">\n                \n                    38\n                \n            </span><span class=\"inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-comments\">COMMENT</span></span><span\n        class=\"inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-email\"\n        data-share-method=\"email\"\n       class=\"inline-share-btn inline-share-btn-more\"\n         data-share-method=\"facebook\"\n         data-uotrack=\"InlineShareMoreBtn\"><span class=\"inline-share-count inline-share-count-more\"></span><span class=\"inline-share-btn-label inline-share-btn-label-more\">MORE</span></span></div></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>A U.S. Secret Service agent who guards Vice President Mike Pence has been suspended after allegedly consorting with a prostitute at a Maryland hotel, CNN and ABC report.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The agency did not immediately respond to an e-mail sent to its press operation Wednesday night.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Both news organizations credited law enforcement sources.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The incident unfolded late last week when the manager of a hotel in Montgomery County, Md., became suspicious about activity in one of the guest rooms and called police, CNN reported. Police saw the agent leave the hotel and stopped him, according to ABC.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>Police arrested the agent for solicitation, and the agent then reported his arrest to the agency, CNN reported.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The agent was off-duty at the time of the incident, both news organizations reported.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>\"The Secret Service takes allegations of criminal activity very seriously,\" the agency said in a statement to ABC. \"This matter is being investigated by our Office of Professional Responsibility to determine the facts.\"</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div class=\"partner-placement partner-spike\"></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The agent turned over his weapon, lost all security clearance and lost access to Secret Service facilities, the New York Daily News reported, citing an agency spokesperson.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>In 2012, Secret Service agents accompanying President Obama on a trip to Colombia allegedly took 20 prostitutes back to their rooms. Eight agents wound up being fired.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div class=\"partner-outstream\"></div><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p>The initial purpose of the agency founded in 1865 was to prevent the production of counterfeit money. Today, the agency's mission is to protect the nation's leaders and to protect the financial and critical infrastructure of the country.</p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><!-- cxenseparse_start --><p><strong>READ MORE:</strong></p><!-- cxenseparse_end --><div id=\"module-position-P2rB7B8Pw-U\" class=\"story-asset oembed-asset\"><div class=\"story-oembed-wrap \"><div \n (Photo: Aaron P. Bernstein, Getty Images)\n\nA U.S. Secret Service agent who guards Vice President Mike Pence has been suspended after allegedly consorting with a prostitute at a Maryland hotel, CNN and ABC report.\n\nThe agency did not immediately respond to an e-mail sent to its press operation Wednesday night.\n\nBoth news organizations credited law enforcement sources.\n\nThe incident unfolded late last week when the manager of a hotel in Montgomery County, Md., became suspicious about activity in one of the guest rooms and called police, CNN reported. Police saw the agent leave the hotel and stopped him, according to ABC.\n\nPolice arrested the agent for solicitation, and the agent then reported his arrest to the agency, CNN reported.\n\nThe agent was off-duty at the time of the incident, both news organizations reported.\n\n\"The Secret Service takes allegations of criminal activity very seriously,\" the agency said in a statement to ABC. \"This matter is being investigated by our Office of Professional Responsibility to determine the facts.\"\n\nThe agent turned over his weapon, lost all security clearance and lost access to Secret Service facilities, the New York Daily News reported, citing an agency spokesperson.\n\nIn 2012, Secret Service agents accompanying President Obama on a trip to Colombia allegedly took 20 prostitutes back to their rooms. Eight agents wound up being fired.\n\nThe initial purpose of the agency founded in 1865 was to prevent the production of counterfeit money. Today, the agency's mission is to protect the nation's leaders and to protect the financial and critical infrastructure of the country.\n\nREAD MORE:\n\nRead or Share this story:
